id="cite_ref-GR3_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Guayama</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;\xc9\xa1wa\xcb\x88\xca\x9dama&#93;</a></span>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991"><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">locally</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;wa\xcb\x88\xca\x9dama&#93;</a></span>), officially the <b>Autonomous Municipality of Guayama</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Municipio Aut\xc3\xb3nomo de Guayama</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Guayama_barrio-pueblo" title="Guayama barrio-pueblo">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean</a> coast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. As of the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 United States Census">2020 U.S. Census</a>, the city had a population of 36,614. It is the center of the <a href="/wiki/Guayama_metropolitan_area" title="Guayama metropolitan area">Guayama metropolitan area</a> with a population of 68,442 in 2020.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology_and_nicknames">Etymology and nicknames</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The original name of the city is <b>San Antonio de Padua de Guayama</b>, named after the saint <a href="/wiki/Anthony_of_Padua" title="Anthony of Padua">Anthony of Padua</a>; as with other settlement names in Puerto Rico, the name was eventually shortened to <i>Guayama</i>. <i>Guayama</i> comes from the name of a <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a> (chief), who was leader of the tribes in the southeastern coast of Puerto Rico. The <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> word <i>Guayama</i> (<i>wayama</i>) is said to mean "great place" or "big open space".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another legend tells that the name of the town comes from the name of a woman called Juana Guayama who is said to have been an early owner of the land around Guayama and granter of the land in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Machete,_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Machete, Guayama, Puerto Rico">Machete</a> where the town was later founded.<sup id="cite_ref-guayamapr.com_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guayamapr.com-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The first nickname of the city was <i>Ciudad del Guaman\xc3\xad</i> ("city of the <a href="/wiki/Guaman%C3%AD_River" title="Guaman\xc3\xad River">Guaman\xc3\xad</a> [River]") after the river that crosses the municipality. The name of this river might be related to the name <i>Guayama</i>, and it has been important to the city since its early founding.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A more modern and more popular nickname for the city is <i>Pueblo de los <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft_in_Latin_America" title="Witchcraft in Latin America">brujos</a></i> ("town of witches" or "town of warlocks") or <i>Pueblo brujo</i> ("witch town"). This nickname traces its origins to a popular story that tells that residents of the city would bring a kind of leaf called <i>hoja bruja</i> ("witch leaf") to <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> games to "scare" the opposing team by pretending to cast spells on them. The town\'s baseball team then adopted the <i>hoja bruja</i> as their symbol.<sup id="cite_ref-guayamapr.com_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guayamapr.com-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another story tells that the nickname comes from a legendary baseball player from the city\'s local team, Moncho El Brujo, who according to legend owed his success as a <a href="/wiki/Pitcher" title="Pitcher">pitcher</a> to witchcraft.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Regardless of the origin of the nickname, residents of Guayama are often called <i>brujos</i> and their <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> team now carries the name <a href="/wiki/Brujos_de_Guayama" title="Brujos de Guayama">Brujos de Guayama</a> ("Guayama Warlocks").<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>During the early years of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonization</a>, the region known today as Guayama was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> native people. The indigenous population in this area decreased due to slavery and migration to the Lesser Antilles. The following centuries, the region was under attack from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno rebellion">Ta\xc3\xadno rebellion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">pirates</a>. The town was founded on January 29, 1736, as <b>San Antonio de Padua de Guayama</b> by then Spanish Governor <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mat%C3%ADas_de_Abad%C3%ADa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mat\xc3\xadas de Abad\xc3\xada (page does not exist)">Mat\xc3\xadas de Abad\xc3\xada</a>, although there is knowledge of it being populated by native people as early as 1567. It was Governor Don Tom\xc3\xa1s de Abad\xc3\xada who officially declared Guayama a "pueblo" (town) with the name of <i>San Antonio de Padua de Guayama</i>. That same year the Catholic church in town, <a href="/wiki/Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua" title="Iglesia de San Antonio de Padua">San Antonio de Padua</a>, was declared a Parish. In 1776, Guayama had 200 houses, the church and a central plaza and the total population was approximately 5,000 villagers. Construction on Guayama\'s Parroquial church of San Antonio de Padua began in 1827 and was completed 40 years later. In 1828 the construction of the King\'s House (Casa del Rey) was completed and the church was rebuilt as well. Earlier that year, Guayama was hit by a terrible fire that destroyed 57 houses and 9 huts. Guayama territorial order was altered at different times through the years. Some of the most populated neighborhoods were segregated to form new towns. <a href="/wiki/Patillas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Patillas, Puerto Rico">Patillas</a> was established in 1811 as an independent municipality. In 1831, the territory comprised the neighborhoods: <a href="/wiki/Algarrobo,_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Algarrobo, Guayama, Puerto Rico">Algarrobos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancones,_Arroyo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ancones, Arroyo, Puerto Rico">Ancones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arroyo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arroyo, Puerto Rico">Arroyo</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carreras,_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carreras, Guayama, Puerto Rico (page does not exist)">Carreras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guayama_barrio-pueblo" title="Guayama barrio-pueblo">Guayama Pueblo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaman%C3%AD" title="Guaman\xc3\xad">Guaman\xc3\xad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jobos,_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jobos, Guayama, Puerto Rico">Jobos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machete,_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Machete, Guayama, Puerto Rico">Machete</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yaurel,_Arroyo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Yaurel, Arroyo, Puerto Rico">Yaurel</a>. Later, Arroyo was divided into Arroyo Este and Arroyo Oeste and neighborhoods emerged: Pozo Hondo, Palmas de Aguamanil, Caimital, Pitajayas, Cuatro Calles, Sabana Eneas, Palmas, and <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a>. The latter had been segregated from <a href="/wiki/Coamo" class="mw-redirect" title="Coamo">Coamo</a>.\n</p><p>In 1855, Arroyo was separated to become an independent municipality, taking the neighborhoods: Ancones, Arroyo, Yaurel, Pitajaya, and Cuatro Calles. By 1878, Guayama was a department head including: <a href="/wiki/Comer%C3%ADo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Comer\xc3\xado, Puerto Rico">Comer\xc3\xado</a> (then Sabana del Palmar), <a href="/wiki/Cidra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cidra, Puerto Rico">Cidra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a>, Salinas, Arroyo, <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Lorenzo, Puerto Rico">San Lorenzo</a> (then called Hato Grande), <a href="/wiki/Aguas_Buenas" class="mw-redirect" title="Aguas Buenas">Aguas Buenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caguas" class="mw-redirect" title="Caguas">Caguas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gurabo, Puerto Rico">Gurabo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Juncos" class="mw-redirect" title="Juncos">Juncos</a>. The development continued with the construction of the town cemetery in 1844, the slaughterhouse and meat market in 1851, and a wooden theater of two levels in 1878. By then Guayama had fourteen sugar plantations operating with steam engines and three with ox mills. Also practiced in this municipality was the exploitation of lead mines by the company "La Estrella", owned by Miguel Planellas, as well as the mineral galena, by the company "La Rosita", owned by Antonio Aponte. In 1881, Guayama is declared a Villa (First Order Municipality).\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a>, American forces under General <a href="/wiki/Nelson_A._Miles" title="Nelson A. Miles">Nelson A. Miles</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica" class="mw-redirect" title="Gu\xc3\xa1nica">Gu\xc3\xa1nica</a> near <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> on July 25, 1898. The landing surprised the United States War Department no less than the Spanish, as Miles had been instructed to land near <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> (the War Department learned of the landing through an Associated Press release.) However, en route to Puerto Rico Miles concluded that a San Juan landing was vulnerable to attack by small boats, and so changed plans. Ponce, said at the time to be the largest city in Puerto Rico, was connected with San Juan by a 110-kilometre (70&#160;mi)  military road, well defended by the Spanish at Coamo and Aibonito. In order to flank this position, American Major General <a href="/wiki/John_R._Brooke" title="John R. Brooke">John R. Brooke</a> landed at Arroyo, just east of Guayama, intending to move on <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a>, which is northwest of Guayama, along the road from Ponce to San Juan. General Brooke occupied Guayama August 5, 1898, after slight opposition, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guayama" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Guayama">Battle of Guayama</a>. On August 9, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guaman%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Guaman\xc3\xad">Battle of Guaman\xc3\xad</a> took place north of Guayama. A more significant battle, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aibonito_Pass" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Aibonito Pass">Battle of Aibonito Pass</a>, was halted on the morning of August 13 upon notification of the armistice between the United States and Spain.\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the United States. In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">United States Department of War</a> conducted a <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Guayama was 12,749.<sup id="cite_ref-OfficeSanger1900_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficeSanger1900-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>After the Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War, Guayama continued to develop. The Bernardini Theater built by engineer Manuel Texidor y Alcal\xc3\xa1 del Olmo opened in 1913. The venue, property of attorney Thomas Bernardini, was the scene for artists of international fame. By that time, Guayama was considered one of the most important cities on the island\'s social scene.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Front_view_of_the_Guayama_Convention_Center.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4f/Front_view_of_the_Guayama_Convention_Center.jpg" decoding="async" width="320" height="213" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="213" /></a><figcaption>Guayama Convention Center</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In the early twentieth century, there were selected societies such as the \'Coliseo Derkes\' and \'Grupo Primavera\', which endowed performing arts as well as scientific events. By the mid-twentieth century, Guayama achieved great industrial development, especially with the establishment of Univis Optical Corp., Angela Manufacturing Company and a petrochemical complex of the <a href="/wiki/Phillips_Petroleum_Company" title="Phillips Petroleum Company">Phillips Petroleum Company</a>. In 1968, the company started production of paraffin, benzene, synthetic fibers, nylon, plastic anhydrous, a 3,800,000 litres (830,000&#160;imp&#160;gal; 1,000,000&#160;US&#160;gal) of gasoline a day, and many other products. During that same decade agriculture began to decline as a result of <a href="/wiki/Land_loss" title="Land loss">land loss</a>, industrialization and the construction of multiple housing developments. The <a href="/wiki/Urban_growth" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban growth">urban growth</a> affected the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane industry">sugar cane industry</a>. However, in 1974, 155,595 tons of sugar cane was harvested in the Municipality producing 12,655 tons of refined sugar.<sup id="cite_ref-Medina-Carrillo_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medina-Carrillo-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2002, AES Puerto Rico opened its <a href="/wiki/Coal_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal power plant">coal power plant</a> in Guayama. The company transmits and distributes electricity through a 25-year contract with the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Electric_Power_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Electric Power Authority">Puerto Rico Electric Power Authority</a>. The 2012 National <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Day_Parade" title="Puerto Rican Day Parade">Puerto Rican Day Parade</a> was dedicated to the Municipality of Guayama and its people.\n</p><p>On September 20, 2017 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck Puerto Rico.  In Guayama, the hurricane triggered numerous landslides and caused major destruction with an estimated 2000 homes losing their roof. The river caused major flooding and people were left with no power.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After Hurricane Maria, the people of Guayama resorted to collecting spring water for their drinking water.<sup id="cite_ref-Baez_Reuters_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baez_Reuters-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cordillera_Central,_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cordillera_Central%2C_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Cordillera_Central%2C_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cordillera_Central%2C_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Cordillera_Central%2C_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cordillera_Central%2C_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Cordillera_Central%2C_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption>View of Guayama, <i>Cordillera Central</i> and Bosque de Carite.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Guayama is located at <span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;params=17.974241_N_66.110034_W_type:city_region:US-PR"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">17\xc2\xb058\xe2\x80\xb227\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb006\xe2\x80\xb236\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">17.974241\xc2\xb0N 66.110034\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">17.974241; -66.110034</span></span></span></a></span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-GR1_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The Municipality of Guayama is located on the Southern Coastal Valley region, bordering the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Patillas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Patillas, Puerto Rico">Patillas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arroyo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arroyo, Puerto Rico">Arroyo</a>. Guayama\'s municipal territory reaches the central mountain range to the north and the Caribbean Sea to the south. The mountain systems <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_J%C3%A1jome" title="Sierra de J\xc3\xa1jome">Sierra de J\xc3\xa1jome</a> (2,395 feet or 730 meters) and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a> cover some of the municipality area. The highest points are the Cerro de la Tabla (2,834 feet or 863 meters) and Cerro Tumbado (2,450 feet or 746 meters), which are part of the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a> mountain system. Other elevations are the mountains Garau, Charcas and Pe\xc3\xb1a Hendida. Parts of the <a href="/wiki/Guavate,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guavate, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Guavate</a>-<a href="/wiki/Carite_State_Forest" title="Carite State Forest">Carite Forest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aguirre_State_Forest" title="Aguirre State Forest">Aguirre State Forest</a> are in Guayama. The Guavate-Carite Forest, a 2,400-hectare (6,000-acre) nature reserve is inhabited by 50 species of birds, making this spot a recognized area for birding and has a reserve with a <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_forest" title="Dwarf forest">dwarf forest</a> that was produced by the region\'s high humidity and moist soil. The Aguirre Forest includes: <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangroves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tidal_flats" class="mw-redirect" title="Tidal flats">tidal flats</a>, bird <a href="/wiki/Rookery" title="Rookery">rookeries</a>, research lakes &amp; large <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_manatee" title="West Indian manatee">manatee</a> population. The <a href="/wiki/Jobos_Bay_National_Estuarine_Research_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Jobos Bay National Estuarine Research Reserve">Jobos Bay National Estuarine Research Reserve</a> was established in 1987. The reserve is located between the coasts of Salinas and Guayama, approximately 1,167 hectares (2,883 acres) of mangrove forest and freshwater wetlands. The two main components: Mar Negro <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove</a> forest, which consists of a mangrove forest and a complex system of lagoons and channels interspersed with salt and mud flats; and Cayos Caribe Islets, which are surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seagrass_meadow" title="Seagrass meadow">seagrass beds</a>, with small beach deposits and upland areas.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Features">Features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>Islands include Cayo Caribes, Isla Morrillito and Mata Redonda.</li>\n<li>Carite Dam</li>\n<li>Gorges; Barros, Brander\xc3\xad, Cimarrona, Coraz\xc3\xb3n, Culebra, Palmas Bajas, and Salada.</li>\n<li>Lakes: Melania Lake, <a href="/wiki/Carite_Lake" title="Carite Lake">Carite Lake</a></li>\n<li>Las Mareas Lagoon</li>\n<li>Rivers: <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Chiquito_(Guayama,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Chiquito (Guayama, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Chiquito</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Guaman%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Guaman\xc3\xad">R\xc3\xado Guaman\xc3\xad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_la_Plata_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de la Plata (Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado de la Plata</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seco_River,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Seco River, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Seco</a>.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The annual precipitation is approximately 1,300 millimetres (52&#160;in)  and the average temperature is 27&#160;\xc2\xb0C (81&#160;\xc2\xb0F).\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:auto; The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pico_1969_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pico_1969-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output 6,959; Caimital 4,124; Carite 1,210; Carmen 619; Guaman\xc3\xad 1,455&#160;; Guayama Pueblo 16,891; Jobos 8,286; Machete 3,846; Palmas 709; Pozo Hondo 1,263; Total 45,362.<sup id="cite_ref-GR2_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR2-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are like <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span>  (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the Commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Guayama: Borinqu\xc3\xa9n, Comunidad Mosquito, Comunidad Puerto de Jobos, Loma del Viento, and Pueblito Del Carmen.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> ("I\'m Touring") campaign, with a passport book and website. The Guayama page lists <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Plaza de Recreo Cristobal Col\xc3\xb3n</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Museo Casa Cuati\xc3\xb1o</i></span>, and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Molino de Vives</i></span>, as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sugar_mill_ruins_in_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption>Sugar mill ruins in Guayama</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:En_la_Ruta_Gastron%C3%B3mica_de_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/En_la_Ruta_Gastron%C3%B3mica_de_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-En_la_Ruta_Gastron%C3%B3mica_de_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/En_la_Ruta_Gastron%C3%B3mica_de_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-En_la_Ruta_Gastron%C3%B3mica_de_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/En_la_Ruta_Gastron%C3%B3mica_de_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-En_la_Ruta_Gastron%C3%B3mica_de_Guayama%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4228" data-file-height="2817" /></a><figcaption>The "gastronomic route" features several restaurants</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In 2015, Guayama launched its "grastromic route", with certified restaurants to meet the needs of tourists and locals alike.<sup id="cite_ref-PH2015_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH2015-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a news article by <a href="/wiki/Primera_Hora_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Primera Hora (Puerto Rico)">Primera Hora</a>, Guayama has 19 beaches including <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Playa el Boh\xc3\xado</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other places of interest in Guayama include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua" title="Iglesia de San Antonio de Padua">San Antonio de Padua Church</a></li>\n<li>Guayama Town Plaza (Plaza p\xc3\xbablica Crist\xc3\xb3bal Col\xc3\xb3n)</li>\n<li>Molino y Hacienda Azucarera Vives</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Casa_Cauti%C3%B1o" title="Casa Cauti\xc3\xb1o">Casa Cauti\xc3\xb1o</a> Museum</li>\n<li>Centro de Bellas Artes</li>\n<li>Teatro Calimano</li>\n<li>First Methodist Church (Built in 1902)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guayama_Convention_Center" title="Guayama Convention Center">Guayama Convention Center</a></li>\n<li>C\xc3\xa9ntrico Mall <sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>El Legado Golf Resort</li>\n<li>Mariposario Las Limas Natural Reserve</li>\n<li>Jobos Bay National Estuarine Research Reserve</li>\n<li>Guavate-<a href="/wiki/Carite_State_Forest" title="Carite State Forest">Carite Forest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aguirre_State_Forest" title="Aguirre State Forest">Aguirre State Forest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carite_Lake" title="Carite Lake">Carite Lake</a></li>\n<li>Pozuelo Beach</li>\n<li>Rodeo Beach</li>\n<li>Fishing Club Guayama</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Industry">Industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Guayama is home to various pharmaceutical and manufacturing companies, such as <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baxter_International" title="Baxter International">Baxter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eli_Lilly" title="Eli Lilly">Eli Lilly</a>, and Tapi. A coal power plant operated by AES.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Health_facilities">Health facilities</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Health facilities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The San Lucas Episcopal Hospital, located on Pedro Albizu Campos Avenue and operated by the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Episcopal Diocese of Puerto Rico">Episcopal Diocese of Puerto Rico</a> and the Santa Rosa Hospital are the main medical facilities in Guayama. The <a href="/wiki/Veterans_Health_Administration" title="Veterans Health Administration">Veterans Health Administration</a> operates a Community-Based Outpatient Clinic (COBC) in the Municipality.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Guayama is the birthplace of numerous artists and musicians who have significantly influenced Puerto Rican culture. During the 20th century, the literary culture of the city was influenced by performers including Afro-Antillano genre poet <a href="/wiki/Luis_Pal%C3%A9s_Matos" title="Luis Pal\xc3\xa9s Matos">Luis Pal\xc3\xa9s Matos</a> and his father Vicente Pal\xc3\xa9s An\xc3\xa9s. Music composer Catalino "Tite" Curet Alonso who became a composer of over 2,000 salsa songs is also from Guayama, even though he was raised in the Santurce section of San Juan. Other performers born in Guayama include actresses Gilda Gal\xc3\xa1n and Karla Monroig. The <a href="/wiki/Casa_Cauti%C3%B1o" title="Casa Cauti\xc3\xb1o">Casa Cauti\xc3\xb1o</a> Museum is administered by the Institute of Puerto Rican Culture and include works of art, wood carvings, sculptures and furniture built by Puerto Rican cabinetmakers for the Cauti\xc3\xb1o family. The museum is listed on the National Register of Historic Places.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Guayama celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in June. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de San Antonio de Padua</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Feria Dulce Sue\xc3\xb1o</i></span> named after a famous Puerto Rican horse is held each March in Guayama. <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Dulce Sue\xc3\xb1o</i></span>, the most influential sire in the modern Puerto Rican <a href="/wiki/Paso_Fino" title="Paso Fino">Paso Fino</a> breed, was born in Guayama.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress)_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress)-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EnciclopediaPR_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EnciclopediaPR-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Guayama include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Witches Carnival \xe2\x80\x93 March</li>\n<li>Guayama Carnival \xe2\x80\x93 April</li>\n<li>Sweet Dreams Fair \xe2\x80\x93 March</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/J%C3%ADbaro_(Puerto_Rico)" title="J\xc3\xadbaro (Puerto Rico)">J\xc3\xadbaro</a> Festival \xe2\x80\x93 October</li>\n<li>Puerto Rican Week \xe2\x80\x93 December</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Guayama had one of the Professional Baseball League founding teams, which won the Championship the first years of the league, 1938\xe2\x80\x9339 and 1939\xe2\x80\x9340. Guayama has a baseball team (Brujos de Guayama) in the <a href="/wiki/Federaci%C3%B3n_de_B%C3%A9isbol_Aficionado_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Federaci\xc3\xb3n de B\xc3\xa9isbol Aficionado de Puerto Rico">Federaci\xc3\xb3n de B\xc3\xa9isbol Aficionado de Puerto Rico</a> that won the national championship in 1987. Guayama also used to have a basketball team in the Puerto Rico\'s <a href="/wiki/Baloncesto_Superior_Nacional" title="Baloncesto Superior Nacional">BSN</a> (Brujos de Guayama) that went to the League finals twice back in 1991 and 1994 but lost both times to eventual champions Atleticos de San German, it was announced that the team will return for the league\'s 2012 season.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Guayama_Convention_Center" title="Guayama Convention Center">Guayama Convention Center</a> hosted some of the roller skating events for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="2010 Central American and Caribbean Games">2010 Central American and Caribbean Games</a> that took place in <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a>, Puerto Rico from July 18, 2010, to August 1, 2010. El Legado Golf Resort, a 285 acres, 18 hole golf course founded in 2002 by Puerto Rican golf player <a href="/wiki/Juan_%22Chi-Chi%22_Rodriguez" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan &quot;Chi-Chi&quot; Rodriguez">Juan "Chi-Chi" Rodriguez</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Guayama_FC" title="Guayama FC">Guayama Football Club</a>, founded in 1949, plays in the <a href="/wiki/Liga_Puerto_Rico" title="Liga Puerto Rico">Liga Puerto Rico</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>As of the 2020 U.S. Census, the city had a population of 36,614. It is the center of the <a href="/wiki/Guayama_metropolitan_area" title="Guayama metropolitan area">Guayama metropolitan area</a>, which was home to 68,442 in 2020.\n</p><p>In terms of race and ethnicity, the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 United States Census">2010 U.S. Census</a> stated the following concerning Guayameses:\n</p>\n<ul><li>White: 72.8% (33,025)</li>\n<li>Black: 22.9% (10,367)</li>\n<li>American Indian/Indigenous: 1.7% (769)</li>\n<li>Asian: 0.2% (108)</li>\n<li>Native Hawaiian/Pacific Islander: 0.1% (51)</li>\n<li>Some Other Race: 8.3.% (3,746)</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The mayor of Guayama as of May, 2022 is O\'Brian V\xc3\xa1zquez Molina.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district VI">Puerto Rico Senatorial district VI</a>, which is represented by two senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Pereira_Castillo" title="Miguel Pereira Castillo">Miguel Pereira Castillo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angel_M._Rodr%C3%ADguez" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel M. Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Angel M. Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> were elected as district senators.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The flag of Guayama is made up of three stripes of different colors: black, yellow, and red from top to bottom. The black stands for the enslaved Africans brought to Puerto Rico, many to Guayama. The yellow represents sugar cane industry in Puerto Rico and the significance of Guayama\'s sugar plantations. The red symbolizes the blood shed by <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> Indians in their fight against the Spanish/European colonizers. To the left of the top stripe we can see the Old Mill, which today is known as the Molino de Vives.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The shield is divided in four parts and in two of them part of a chessboard appears. The chessboard pattern represents the center of the city, which resembles a chessboard. It has two old mill towers. The laurel trees constitute a representation of the beautiful Recreation Plaza very well known for its trimmed trees. The three silver flowers symbolize San Antonio de Padua, patron of Guayama. The crown represents Cacique Guayama, name of the town. The big crown has four towers.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The education system in Guayama has three public high schools, which are Francisco Garcia Boyrie, Adela Brenes Texidor and Dr. Rafael Lopez Landr\xc3\xb3n, and one vocational high school, Dra. Maria Socorro Lacot. Guayama also has a campus of the Puerto Rico Institute of Technology and the <a href="/wiki/Inter_American_University_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Inter American University of Puerto Rico">Inter American University of Puerto Rico</a>, Guayama campus (<i>Universidad Interamericana de Puerto Rico, Recinto de Guayama</i> in Spanish) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.guayama.inter.edu/">Universidad Interamericana de Puerto Rico \xe2\x80\x93 Recinto de Guayama</a>\n. It also has several private schools such as Academia San Antonio, Guaman\xc3\xad Private School, Saint Patrick\'s Bilingual School, Colegio Cat\xc3\xb2lico San Antonio, Fountain Christian Bilingual School, Escuela Superior and Academia Adventista Tres Angeles and more than 12 other public schools in the elementary and intermediate education levels.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Guayama is served by multiple state highways, principally <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_54" title="Puerto Rico Highway 54">Puerto Rico Highway 54</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_53" title="Puerto Rico Highway 53">Puerto Rico Highway 53</a>, PR-3, PR-15, PR-179, PR-744, PR-748, and PR-7710. PR-54 serves as a <i>by-pass</i> route to PR-3 which crosses the <i>pueblo</i>. PR-54 also serves as the main route towards PR-53, connecting Guayama to the neighboring town of Salinas and PR-52, providing expressway access towards Ponce, San Juan, and Caguas. Just north of the Guayama <i>barrio-pueblo</i> is PR-748, which, along with the <i>Conector Dulce Sue\xc3\xb1o</i> forms a ring around Guayama\xe2\x80\x99s urban area. PR-748 intercepts Olimpo and Caimital, eventually intersecting with the rural PR-15, connecting Guayama with Cayey. PR-179 is born out of PR-15, serving as the main route through barrios Guaman\xc3\xad and Carite until its intersection with PR-184 in Cayey. Just south of Guayama\xe2\x80\x99s main urban area, PR-3 continues on its way to Salinas. It crosses through Jobos, right in front of its parish and continues to Salinas. PR-7710 serves as the only route to the coastal sector of Pozuelo, offering some of the best beaches Guayama has to offer. The Municipality is only 38&#160;mi (61&#160;km) away from <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> and 58&#160;mi (93&#160;km) from San Juan via expressways PR-53 and PR-52. The nearest international airport is the <a href="/wiki/Mercedita_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedita Airport">Mercedita Airport</a> in Ponce.\n</p><p>At one time during 1937, Guayama received domestic, commercial airline flights from San Juan on Puerto Rico\'s national airline, <a href="/wiki/Puertorrique%C3%B1a_de_Aviaci%C3%B3n" title="Puertorrique\xc3\xb1a de Aviaci\xc3\xb3n">Puertorrique\xc3\xb1a de Aviaci\xc3\xb3n</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>There are 28 bridges in Guayama.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_Guayameses">Notable <i>Guayameses</i></h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guayama,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notable Guayameses"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Category:People from Guayama, Puerto Rico">Category:People from Guayama, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<ul><li>Jose C. Aponte Garcia - Puerto Rico Prosecuting Attorney during the Administrations of Luis Munoz Marin, Roberto Sanchez Vilella; Secretary of Justice during Roberto Sanchez Vilella\'s Administration</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Modesto_Cartagena" title="Modesto Cartagena">Modesto Cartagena</a> - Purple Heart recipient</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tite_Curet_Alonso" title="Tite Curet Alonso">Catalino (Tite) Curet Alonso</a> - composer of over 2,000 salsa songs.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Diosa_Costello" title="Diosa Costello">Diosa Costello</a> - actress, AKA: The Original Latin Bombshell. True Name: Juana de Dios Castrello</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Luis_Pal%C3%A9s_Matos" title="Luis Pal\xc3\xa9s Matos">Luis Pal\xc3\xa9s Matos</a> - Puerto Rican poet who is credited with creating the poetry genre known as Afro-Antillano.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gilda_Gal%C3%A1n" title="Gilda Gal\xc3\xa1n">Gilda Gal\xc3\xa1n</a> - Puerto Rican actress, dramaticist, comedian, writer, composer, scriptwriter and poet.<sup id="cite_ref-vocero_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vocero-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rafael_P%C3%A9rez_Perry" title="Rafael P\xc3\xa9rez Perry">Rafael P\xc3\xa9rez Perry</a> - Businessman and a pioneer in Puerto Rico\'s radio and television broadcasting industry. In 1954 founded Puerto Rico\'s television Channel 11 (nowadays <a href="/wiki/Univision_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Univision Puerto Rico">Univision Puerto Rico</a>).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Miguel_Poventud" title="Miguel Poventud">Miguel Poventud</a> - Puerto Rican musician, singer, actor and composer of Boleros.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pedro_Garc%C3%ADa_(baseball)" title="Pedro Garc\xc3\xada (baseball)">Pedro Garcia</a> - Major League Baseball player for the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Karla_Monroig" title="Karla Monroig">Karla Monroig</a> - Telenovela actress, model and television host.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roger_Moret" title="Roger Moret">Roger Moret</a>- Former <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> pitcher</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Juan_Laporte" title="Juan Laporte">Juan Laporte</a> -Former WBC featherweight boxing champion (1982\xe2\x80\x931984)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jaime_Fuster_Berlingeri" class="mw-redirect" title="Jaime Fuster Berlingeri">Jaime Fuster Berlingeri</a>- Associate Justice to the Supreme Court of Puerto Rico and former Resident Commissioner to the U.S. Congress.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marcos_Crespo" title="Marcos Crespo">Marcos Crespo</a> - Democratic member of the New York State Assembly representing the 85th Assembly District.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carmelo_Delgado_Delgado" title="Carmelo Delgado Delgado">Carmelo Delgado Delgado</a> - Leader of the Puerto Rican Nationalist Party. Is thought to be the first U.S. citizen to die in Spain\'s civil war.</li>\n<li>Dr.<a href="/wiki/Victor_Manuel_Blanco" class="mw-redirect" title="Victor Manuel Blanco">Victor Manuel Blanco</a> PhD - Scientist and astronomer who in 1959 discovered "Blanco 1," a galactic cluster.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eddie_Rosario" title="Eddie Rosario">Eddie Rosario</a> - Major League Baseball player for the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> and was the <a href="/wiki/2021_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="2021 NLCS">2021 NLCS</a> <a href="/wiki/League_Championship_Series_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="League Championship Series Most Valuable Player Award">MVP</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_Santiago_Lavandero" title="Leopoldo Santiago Lavandero">Leopoldo Santiago Lavandero</a> (1912-2003) - playwright, theater producer and teacher.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plan_B_(duo)" title="Plan B (duo)">Plan B</a> - reggaet\xc3\xb3n duo with multiple songs on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Latin_Songs" title="Hot Latin Songs">Billboard Hot Latin Songs</a> charts.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ricky_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Ricky S\xc3\xa1nchez">Ricky S\xc3\xa1nchez</a> - Former basketball player, drafted by the <a href="/wiki/Portland_Trail_Blazers" title="Portland Trail Blazers">Portland Trail Blazers</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_NBA_draft" title="2005 NBA draft">2005</a>.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Gallery">Gallery</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span
